            <section ID="LINK_a8e87156-1790-4479-b994-930898fd7c9e">
               <id root="12f59056-6932-4820-89ac-5c62da6f3884"/>
               <code code="34066-1" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="BOXED WARNING SECTION"/>
               <title>
                  <content styleCode="bold">WARNING: SERIOUS ADVERSE REACTIONS INCLUDING TENDINITIS, TENDON RUPTURE, PERIPHERAL NEUROPATHY, CENTRAL NERVOUS SYSTEM EFFECTS AND EXACERBATION OF MYASTHENIA GRAVIS</content>
               </title>
               <text>
                  <paragraph>
                     <content styleCode="bold">
                        <content styleCode="xmChange">- Fluoroquinolones, including levofloxacin, have been associated with disabling and potentially irreversible serious adverse reactions that have occurred together [see Warnings and Precautions (</content>
                        <content styleCode="xmChange">
                           <linkHtml href="#LINK_0991ea01-74a1-403b-851a-36a06ec4872e">5.1</linkHtml>
                        </content>
                        <content styleCode="xmChange">)], including:</content>
                     </content>
                  </paragraph>
                  <list listType="unordered" styleCode="Circle">
                     <item>
                        <content styleCode="bold">
                           <content styleCode="xmChange">Tendinitis and tendon rupture [see Warnings and Precautions (</content>
                           <content styleCode="xmChange">
                              <linkHtml href="#LINK_10b867ee-c48f-4bef-8c8f-e9bd9f0ff6ba">5.2</linkHtml>
                           </content>
                           <content styleCode="xmChange">)]</content>
                        </content>
                     </item>
                     <item>
                        <content styleCode="bold">
                           <content styleCode="xmChange">Peripheral neuropathy [see Warnings and Precautions (</content>
                           <content styleCode="xmChange">
                              <linkHtml href="#LINK_7a390283-f0a5-4bf0-9f4a-be9c29fd2fcb">5.3</linkHtml>
                           </content>
                           <content styleCode="xmChange">)]</content>
                        </content>
                     </item>
                     <item>
                        <content styleCode="bold">
                           <content styleCode="xmChange">Central nervous system effects [see Warnings and Precautions (</content>
                           <content styleCode="xmChange">
                              <linkHtml href="#LINK_da68872a-681b-4f73-8c30-8e6138e65875">5.4</linkHtml>
                           </content>
                           <content styleCode="xmChange">)]</content>
                        </content>
                     </item>
                  </list>
                  <paragraph>
                     <content styleCode="bold">
                        <content styleCode="xmChange">Discontinue levofloxacin immediately and avoid the use of fluoroquinolones, including levofloxacin, in patients who experience any of these serious adverse reactions [see Warnings and Precautions (</content>
                        <content styleCode="xmChange">
                           <linkHtml href="#LINK_0991ea01-74a1-403b-851a-36a06ec4872e">5.1</linkHtml>
                        </content>
                        <content styleCode="xmChange">)]</content>
                     </content>
                  </paragraph>
                  <paragraph>
                     <content styleCode="bold">
                        <content styleCode="xmChange">- Fluoroquinolones, including levofloxacin, may exacerbate muscle weakness in patients with myasthenia gravis. Avoid levofloxacin in patients with a known history of myasthenia gravis [see Warnings and Precautions (</content>
                        <content styleCode="xmChange">
                           <linkHtml href="#LINK_aaee3dd2-757e-45de-815b-91e5d8b415e6">5.5</linkHtml>
                        </content>
                        <content styleCode="xmChange">)].</content>
                     </content>
                  </paragraph>
                  <paragraph>
                     <content styleCode="bold">
                        <content styleCode="xmChange">- Because fluoroquinolones, including levofloxacin, have been associated with serious adverse reactions [see Warnings and Precautions (</content>
                        <content styleCode="xmChange">
                           <linkHtml href="#LINK_f73e3b6b-e858-46c7-96ed-1edbbce99943">5.1-5.14</linkHtml>
                        </content>
                        <content styleCode="xmChange">)], reserve levofloxacin for use in patients who have no alternative treatment options for the following indications:</content>
                     </content>
                  </paragraph>
                  <list listType="unordered" styleCode="Circle">
                     <item>
                        <content styleCode="bold">
                           <content styleCode="xmChange">Uncomplicated urinary tract infection [see Indications and Usage (</content>

                           </content>
                           <content styleCode="xmChange">)]</content>
                        </content>
                     </item>

               <excerpt>
                  <highlight>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>
                           <content styleCode="bold">WARNING: </content>
                           <content styleCode="bold">SERIOUS ADVERSE REACTIONS INCLUDING TENDINITIS, TENDON RUPTURE, PERIPHERAL NEUROPATHY, CENTRAL NERVOUS SYSTEM EFFECTS AND EXACERBATION OF MYASTHENIA GRAVIS</content>
                        </paragraph>
                        <paragraph>
                           <content styleCode="italics">
                              <content styleCode="bold">See full prescribing information for complete boxed warning.</content>
                           </content>
                        </paragraph>
                        <list listType="unordered" styleCode="Disk">
                           <item>
                              <content styleCode="bold">Fluoroquinolones, including levofloxacin, have been associated with disabling and potentially irreversible serious adverse reactions that have occurred together (<linkHtml href="#LINK_0991ea01-74a1-403b-851a-36a06ec4872e">5.1</linkHtml>), including:</content>
                              <list listType="unordered" styleCode="Circle">
                                 <item>
                                    <content styleCode="bold">Tendinitis and tendon rupture (<linkHtml href="#LINK_10b867ee-c48f-4bef-8c8f-e9bd9f0ff6ba">5.2</linkHtml>)</content>
                                 </item>
                                 <item>
                                    <content styleCode="bold">Peripheral neuropathy (<linkHtml href="#LINK_7a390283-f0a5-4bf0-9f4a-be9c29fd2fcb">5.3</linkHtml>)</content>
                                 </item>
                                 <item>
                                    <content styleCode="bold">Central nervous system effects (<linkHtml href="#LINK_da68872a-681b-4f73-8c30-8e6138e65875">5.4</linkHtml>) </content>
                                 </item>
                              </list>
                           </item>
                        </list>
                        <paragraph>
                           <content styleCode="bold">Discontinue levofloxacin immediately and avoid the use of fluoroquinolones, including levofloxacin, in patients who experience any of these serious adverse reactions (<linkHtml href="#LINK_0991ea01-74a1-403b-851a-36a06ec4872e">5.1</linkHtml>).</content>
                        </paragraph>
                        <list listType="unordered" styleCode="Disc">
                           <item>
                              <content styleCode="bold">Fluoroquinolones, including levofloxacin, may exacerbate muscle weakness in patients with myasthenia gravis. Avoid levofloxacin in patients with a known history of myasthenia gravis [see Warnings and Precautions (<linkHtml href="#LINK_aaee3dd2-757e-45de-815b-91e5d8b415e6">5.5</linkHtml>)].</content>
                           </item>
                           <item>
                              <content styleCode="bold">Because fluoroquinolones, including levofloxacin, have been associated with serious adverse reactions (<linkHtml href="#LINK_f73e3b6b-e858-46c7-96ed-1edbbce99943">5.1-5.14</linkHtml>), reserve levofloxacin for use in </content>
                              <content styleCode="bold">patients who have no alternative treatment options for the following indications: </content>
                              <list listType="unordered" styleCode="Circle">
                                 <item>
                                    <content styleCode="bold">Uncomplicated urinary tract infection (<linkHtml href="#LINK_681c4997-2c01-4b8a-81cb-03b1e4e47da2">1.12</linkHtml>) </content>
                                 </item>
                                 <item>
                                    <content styleCode="bold">Acute bacterial exacerbation of chronic bronchitis (<linkHtml href="#LINK_c6c7d68d-c7d3-4be1-94e6-45436f186678">1.13</linkHtml>)</content>

                                    <content styleCode="bold">Acute bacterial sinusitis (<linkHtml href="#LINK_0d91e8dc-a950-4bdd-92b8-b2629df2dbb3">1.14</linkHtml>)</content>
                                 </item>
                              </list>

                        </list>

               <code code="34067-9" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="INDICATIONS &amp; USAGE SECTION"/>
               <title>1 INDICATIONS AND USAGE</title>
               <text>
                  <paragraph>Levofloxacin injection is indicated for the treatment of adults (â¥ 18 years of age) with mild, moderate, and severe infections caused by susceptible isolates of the designated microorganisms in the conditions listed in this section. Levofloxacin injection is indicated when intravenous administration offers a route of administration advantageous to the patient (e.g., patient cannot tolerate an oral dosage form).</paragraph>
               </text>
               <effectiveTime value="20160816"/>
               <excerpt>
                  <highlight>
                     <text>

</item>
                           <item>Skin and skin structure infections: complicated (<linkHtml href="#LINK_e61644b5-b3b1-49d8-a1ee-cbc913b2203f">1.4</linkHtml>) and uncomplicated (<linkHtml href="#LINK_68a329b8-50a0-4fa4-84ed-afd0b7cbfe3e">1.5</linkHtml>)</item>

                        <paragraph>Levofloxacin is indicated for the treatment of nosocomial pneumonia due to methicillin-susceptible <content styleCode="italics">Staphylococcus aureus</content>, <content styleCode="italics">Pseudomonas aeruginosa</content>, <content styleCode="italics">Serratia marcescens</content>, <content styleCode="italics">Escherichia coli</content>, <content styleCode="italics">Klebsiella pneumoniae</content>, <content styleCode="italics">Haemophilus influenzae</content>, or <content styleCode="italics">Streptococcus pneumoniae</content>. Adjunctive therapy should be used as clinically indicated. Where <content styleCode="italics">Pseudomonas aeruginosa</content> is a documented or presumptive pathogen, combination therapy with an anti-pseudomonal Î²-lactam is recommended [see <content styleCode="bold">CLINICAL STUDIES (<linkHtml href="#LINK_20b92eae-b505-4e25-a012-6b7ea12bab25">14.1</linkHtml>)</content>].</paragraph>
                     </text>

                     <id root="7b1fda56-7060-4633-9355-8caf99d2ce2a"/>
                     <code code="42229-5" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="SPL UNCLASSIFIED SECTION"/>
                     <title>
                        <content styleCode="bold">

1.7 Inhalational Anthrax (Post-Exposure)</content>
                     </title>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>Levofloxacin is indicated for inhalational anthrax (post-exposure) to reduce the incidence or progression of disease following exposure to aerosolized <content styleCode="italics">Bacillus anthracis. </content>The effectiveness of levofloxacin is based on plasma concentrations achieved in humans, a surrogate endpoint reasonably likely to predict clinical benefit. Levofloxacin has not been tested in humans for the post-exposure prevention of inhalation anthrax. The safety of levofloxacin in adults for durations of therapy beyond 28 days or in pediatric patients for durations of therapy beyond 14 days has not been studied. Prolonged levofloxacin therapy should only be used when the benefit outweighs the risk [see <content styleCode="bold">DOSAGE AND ADMINISTRATION (<linkHtml href="#LINK_d3ea19ca-1e35-40d0-8e9b-37c2e8a4a0d8">2.1</linkHtml>, <linkHtml href="#LINK_074c7e76-37c8-48ae-bf26-f7ff41b1d00b">2.2</linkHtml>); </content>
                           <content styleCode="bold">CLINICAL STUDIES (<linkHtml href="#LINK_eda5db73-92cb-4927-9490-0ee79d298e57">14.9</linkHtml>)</content>]<content styleCode="italics">.</content>
                        </paragraph>
                     </text>

                     <title>
                        <content styleCode="bold">

1.8 Plague</content>
                     </title>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>Levofloxacin is indicated for treatment of plague, including pneumonic and septicemic plague, due to <content styleCode="italics">Yersinia pestis</content> (<content styleCode="italics">Y. pestis</content>) and prophylaxis for plague in adults and pediatric patients, 6 months of age and older. Efficacy studies of levofloxacin could not be conducted in humans with plague for ethical and feasibility reasons. Therefore, approval of this indication was based on an efficacy study conducted in animals [see <content styleCode="bold">DOSAGE AND ADMINISTRATION (<linkHtml href="#LINK_d3ea19ca-1e35-40d0-8e9b-37c2e8a4a0d8">2.1</linkHtml>, <linkHtml href="#LINK_074c7e76-37c8-48ae-bf26-f7ff41b1d00b">2.2</linkHtml>)</content> and <content styleCode="bold">CLINICAL STUDIES (<linkHtml href="#LINK_61466cb7-0624-4e2a-8190-17b69bbd3bfb">14.10</linkHtml>)</content>].</paragraph>
                     </text>

                  <section ID="LINK_0e2f16a6-0ea9-4dff-8efb-27cb1d9b40c2">
                     <id root="b8a773de-38f6-4b4a-96e2-bcdf4872acb9"/>
                     <code code="42229-5" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="SPL UNCLASSIFIED SECTION"/>
                     <title>
                        <content styleCode="bold">1.11 Acute Pyelonephritis: 5 or 10-day Treatment Regimen</content>
                     </title>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>Levofloxacin is indicated for the treatment of acute pyelonephritis caused by <content styleCode="italics">Escherichia coli</content>, including cases with concurrent bacteremia [see <content styleCode="bold">CLINICAL STUDIES (<linkHtml href="#LINK_2ef23ab7-6006-481b-8fc4-08bca9b2655c">14.7</linkHtml>, <linkHtml href="#LINK_f00de8b2-e8fa-4e23-aaa7-36a8a642f8fb">14.8</linkHtml>)</content>].</paragraph>
                     </text>
                     <effectiveTime value="20130801"/>
                  </section>
               </component>
               <component>
                  <section ID="LINK_681c4997-2c01-4b8a-81cb-03b1e4e47da2">
                     <id root="238a41c8-3ebc-4b20-8159-88ce8895e465"/>
                     <code code="42229-5" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="SPL UNCLASSIFIED SECTION"/>
                     <title>
                        <content styleCode="bold">1.12 Uncomplicated Urinary Tract Infections</content>
                     </title>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>Levofloxacin is indicated for the treatment of uncomplicated urinary tract infections (mild to moderate) due to <content styleCode="italics">Escherichia coli, Klebsiella pneumoniae, </content>or<content styleCode="italics"> Staphylococcus saprophyticus</content>.</paragraph>
                        <paragraph>
                           <content styleCode="xmChange">Because fluoroquinolones, including levofloxacin, have been associated with serious adverse reactions [see <content styleCode="bold">WARNINGS AND PRECAUTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_f73e3b6b-e858-46c7-96ed-1edbbce99943">5.1-5.14</linkHtml>)</content>] and for some patients uncomplicated urinary tract infection is self-limiting, reserve levofloxacin for treatment of uncomplicated urinary tract infections in patients who have no alternative treatment options.</content>
                        </paragraph>
                     </text>
                     <effectiveTime value="20160816"/>
                  </section>
               </component>
               <component>
                  <section ID="LINK_c6c7d68d-c7d3-4be1-94e6-45436f186678">
                     <id root="77b2dbcc-60cf-4b27-8f76-525ca70c674f"/>
                     <code code="42229-5" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="SPL UNCLASSIFIED SECTION"/>
                     <title>
                        <content styleCode="bold">1.13 Acute Bacterial Exacerbation of Chronic
Bronchitis</content>
                     </title>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>Levofloxacin is indicated for the treatment of acute bacterial exacerbation of chronic bronchitis (ABECB) due to methicillinâsusceptible <content styleCode="italics">Staphylococcus aureus</content>, <content styleCode="italics">Streptococcus pneumoniae, Haemophilus influenzae, Haemophilus parainfluenzae, </content>or <content styleCode="italics">Moraxella catarrhalis</content>.</paragraph>
                        <paragraph>
                           <content styleCode="xmChange">Because fluoroquinolones, including levofloxacin, have been associated with serious adverse reactions [see <content styleCode="bold">WARNINGS AND PRECAUTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_f73e3b6b-e858-46c7-96ed-1edbbce99943">5.1-5.14</linkHtml>)</content>]and for some patients ABECB is self-limiting, reserve levofloxacin for treatment of ABECB in patients who have no alternative treatment options.</content>
                        </paragraph>
                     </text>
                     <effectiveTime value="20160816"/>
                  </section>
               </component>
               <component>
                  <section ID="LINK_0d91e8dc-a950-4bdd-92b8-b2629df2dbb3">
                     <id root="24f3be2b-22aa-4b82-80f4-701e926317ad"/>
                     <code code="42229-5" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="SPL UNCLASSIFIED SECTION"/>
                     <title>
                        <content styleCode="bold">

1.14 Acute Bacterial Sinusitis: 5-day and 10â14 day
Treatment Regimens</content>
                     </title>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>Levofloxacin is indicated for the treatment of acute bacterial sinusitis (ABS) due to <content styleCode="italics">Streptococcus pneumoniae</content>, <content styleCode="italics">Haemophilus influenzae, </content>or<content styleCode="italics"> Moraxella catarrhalis </content>[see <content styleCode="bold">CLINICAL STUDIES (<linkHtml href="#LINK_48f57bf0-9a7c-4dd5-b0da-db93a6a42881">14.4</linkHtml>)</content>].</paragraph>
                        <paragraph>
                           <content styleCode="xmChange">Because fluoroquinolones, including levofloxacin, have been associated with serious adverse reactions [see <content styleCode="bold">WARNINGS AND PRECAUTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_f73e3b6b-e858-46c7-96ed-1edbbce99943">5.1-5.14</linkHtml>)</content>] and for some patients ABS is self-limiting, reserve levofloxacin for treatment of ABS in patients who have no alternative treatment options.</content>
                        </paragraph>
                     </text>
                     <effectiveTime value="20160816"/>
                  </section>
               </component>
               <component>
                  <section ID="LINK_a7b84a38-d1da-4248-8f0b-6cc263a3ba3e">
                     <id root="19ce1ed1-bb5f-4283-8e47-41e9159fb200"/>
                     <code code="42229-5" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="SPL UNCLASSIFIED SECTION"/>
                     <title>
                        <content styleCode="bold">1.15 Usage</content>
                     </title>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>To reduce the development of drug-resistant bacteria and maintain the effectiveness of levofloxacin and other antibacterial drugs, levofloxacin should be used only to treat or prevent infections that are proven or strongly suspected to be caused by susceptible bacteria. When culture and susceptibility information are available, they should be considered in selecting or modifying antibacterial therapy. In the absence of such data, local epidemiology and susceptibility patterns may contribute to the empiric selection of therapy.</paragraph>
                        <paragraph>
                           <content styleCode="bold">Culture and susceptibility testing<br/>
                           </content>Appropriate culture and susceptibility tests should be performed before treatment in order to isolate and identify organisms causing the infection and to determine their susceptibility to levofloxacin [see <content styleCode="bold">MICROBIOLOGY (<linkHtml href="#LINK_ed3d8a3b-5eb5-4634-9172-3959fba7ebda">12.4</linkHtml>)</content>]. Therapy with levofloxacin may be initiated before results of these tests are known; once results become available, appropriate therapy should be selected.</paragraph>
                        <paragraph>As with other drugs in this class, some isolates of <content styleCode="italics">Pseudomonas aeruginosa</content> may develop resistance fairly rapidly during treatment with levofloxacin. Culture and susceptibility testing performed periodically during therapy will provide information about the continued susceptibility of the pathogens to the antimicrobial agent and also the possible emergence of bacterial resistance.</paragraph>
                     </text>
                     <effectiveTime value="20160815"/>
                  </section>
               </component>
            </section>
         </component>

                           <sup>9</sup> Drug administration should begin as soon as possible after suspected or confirmed exposure to <content styleCode="italics">Yersinia pestis</content>.Â Higher doses of levofloxacin typically used for treatment of pneumonia can be used for treatment of plague, if clinically indicated.</paragraph>

                        <content styleCode="bold">2.3 Dosage Adjustment in Adults with Renal Impairment</content>
                     </title>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>Administer levofloxacin with caution in the presence of renal insufficiency. Careful clinical observation and appropriate laboratory studies should be performed prior to and during therapy since elimination of levofloxacin may be reduced.</paragraph>
                        <paragraph>No adjustment is necessary for patients with a creatinine clearance â¥ 50 mL/min.</paragraph>
                        <paragraph>In patients with impaired renal function (creatinine clearance &lt; 50 mL/min), adjustment of the dosage regimen is necessary to avoid the accumulation of levofloxacin due to decreased clearance [see <content styleCode="bold">USE IN SPECIFIC POPULATIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_7e047670-63c8-4b2f-9dda-d2261568eaa3">8.6</linkHtml>)</content>]<content styleCode="italics">.</content>

               <component>
                  <section ID="LINK_c66ccf10-2cdb-4177-a8c1-87592e9d2b62">
                     <id root="c6015af4-ed5f-4b82-92cc-0d8549070ead"/>
                     <code code="42229-5" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="SPL UNCLASSIFIED SECTION"/>
                     <title>
                        <content styleCode="bold">2.5 Administration Instructions</content>
                     </title>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>
                           <content styleCode="bold">Levofloxacin Injection <br/>
                           </content>Caution: Rapid or bolus intravenous infusion of levofloxacin has been associated with hypotension and must be avoided. Levofloxacin injection should be infused intravenously slowly over a period of not less than 60 or 90 minutes, depending on the dosage. Levofloxacin injection should be administered only by intravenous infusion. It is not for intramuscular, intrathecal, intraperitoneal, or subcutaneous administration.</paragraph>
                        <paragraph>
                           <content styleCode="bold">Hydration for Patients Receiving Levofloxacin Injection <br/>
                           </content>Adequate hydration of patients receiving intravenous levofloxacin should be maintained to prevent the formation of highly concentrated urine. Crystalluria and cylindruria have been reported with quinolones [see <content styleCode="bold">ADVERSE REACTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_38344cce-d4d7-4566-8a4a-28ff594d1902">6.1</linkHtml>)</content>; <content styleCode="bold">PATIENT COUNSELING INFORMATION (<linkHtml href="#LINK_758ffc71-e10b-4ebd-a010-25ce6bbd7f8d">17.2</linkHtml>)</content>]<content styleCode="italics">.</content>
                        </paragraph>
                     </text>
                     <effectiveTime value="20160816"/>
                  </section>
               </component>
               <component>
                  <section ID="LINK_03cd1151-5874-4992-91b2-e26387b8c6da">
                     <id root="b8da869c-fd14-4ab9-b2cc-5b821000deda"/>
                     <code code="42229-5" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="SPL UNCLASSIFIED SECTION"/>
                     <title>
                        <content styleCode="bold">2.6 Preparation of Intravenous Product</content>
                     </title>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>Parenteral drug products should be inspected visually for particulate matter and discoloration prior to administration, whenever solution and container permit.</paragraph>
                        <paragraph>Because only limited data are available on the compatibility of levofloxacin injection with other intravenous substances, additives or other medications should not be added to Levofloxacin Injection Premix in Single Dose Flexible Containers, or infused simultaneously through the same intravenous line. If the same intravenous line is used for sequential infusion of several different drugs, the line should be flushed before and after infusion of levofloxacin injection with an infusion solution compatible with levofloxacin injection and with any other drug(s) administered via this common line.</paragraph>
                        <paragraph>
                           <content styleCode="bold">Levofloxacin Injection Premix in Single Dose Flexible Containers (5 mg/mL)<br/>
                           </content>Levofloxacin injection is supplied in flexible containers within a foil overwrap. These contain a premixed, ready to use levofloxacin solution in 5% dextrose (D5W) for single dose. The 50 mL premixed flexible containers contain 250Â mg/50Â mL, the 100 mL premixed flexible containers contain 500 mg/100 mL, and the 200 mL premixed flexible containers contain 750 mg/150 mL of levofloxacin solution. The concentration of each container is 5 mg/mL. No further dilution of these preparations is necessary. Because the premix flexible containers are for single dose only, any unused portion should be discarded.</paragraph>
                        <paragraph>
                           <content styleCode="underline">Instructions for the Use of Levofloxacin Injection Premix in Flexible Containers</content>:</paragraph>
                        <list listType="ordered" styleCode="Arabic">
                           <item>Tear outer wrap at the notch and remove solution container.Â  

</item>
                           <item>Check the container for minute leaks by squeezing the inner bag firmly. If leaks are found, or if the seal is not intact, discard the solution, as the sterility may be compromised. 

</item>
                           <item>Do not use if the solution is cloudy or a precipitate is present. 

</item>
                           <item>Use sterile equipment. 

</item>
                           <item>
                              <content styleCode="bold">WARNING: Do not use flexible containers in series connections.</content> Such use could result in air embolism due to residual air being drawn from the primary container before administration of the fluid from the secondary container is complete. </item>
                        </list>
                        <paragraph>
                           <content styleCode="underline">Preparation for Administration</content>:</paragraph>
                        <list listType="ordered" styleCode="Arabic">
                           <item>Close flow control clamp of administration set. </item>
                           <item>Remove cover from port at bottom of container. </item>
                           <item>Insert piercing pin of administration set into port with a twisting motion until the pin is firmly seated. <content styleCode="bold">NOTE: See full directions on administration set carton.</content>
                           </item>
                           <item>Suspend container from hanger. </item>
                           <item>Squeeze and release drip chamber to establish proper fluid level in chamber during infusion of Levofloxacin Injection Premix in Flexible Containers. </item>
                           <item>Open flow control clamp to expel air from set. Close clamp. </item>
                           <item>Regulate rate of administration with flow control clamp. </item>
                        </list>
                     </text>
                     <effectiveTime value="20141007"/>
                  </section>
               </component>

                                    </paragraph>
                                 </td>
                              </tr>
                              <tr>
                                 <td styleCode="     Botrule          Toprule         Lrule          Rrule     " valign="top">
                                    <paragraph>Injection: premix single dose flexible containers</paragraph>

                     </text>

            <section ID="LINK_ee48c310-f899-46d5-8513-3f5b635aa4f4">
               <id root="d6de5a85-69d0-43af-9633-8aad4c71aa2b"/>
               <code code="34070-3" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="CONTRAINDICATIONS SECTION"/>
               <title>4 CONTRAINDICATIONS</title>
               <text>
                  <paragraph>Levofloxacin is contraindicated in persons with known hypersensitivity to levofloxacin, or other quinolone antibacterials [see <content styleCode="bold">WARNINGS AND PRECAUTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_1bd7e834-3bbd-47b6-9794-f13e51b6b1e7">5.3</linkHtml>)</content>].</paragraph>
               </text>
               <effectiveTime value="20160815"/>
               <excerpt>
                  <highlight>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>Known hypersensitivity to levofloxacin or other quinolones (<linkHtml href="#LINK_ee48c310-f899-46d5-8513-3f5b635aa4f4">4</linkHtml>, <linkHtml href="#LINK_1bd7e834-3bbd-47b6-9794-f13e51b6b1e7">5.7</linkHtml>)</paragraph>
                     </text>
                  </highlight>
               </excerpt>

         <component>
            <section ID="LINK_f73e3b6b-e858-46c7-96ed-1edbbce99943">
               <id root="c81193b0-3684-4393-956f-0a028baf81ab"/>
               <code code="43685-7" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="WARNINGS AND PRECAUTIONS SECTION"/>
               <title>5 WARNINGS AND PRECAUTIONS</title>
               <effectiveTime value="20160816"/>
               <excerpt>
                  <highlight>
                     <text>
                        <list listType="unordered" styleCode="Disk">
                           <item>Anaphylactic reactions and allergic skin reactions, serious, occasionally fatal, may occur after first dose (<linkHtml href="#LINK_ee48c310-f899-46d5-8513-3f5b635aa4f4">4</linkHtml>, <linkHtml href="#LINK_1bd7e834-3bbd-47b6-9794-f13e51b6b1e7">5.7</linkHtml>) </item>
                           <item>Hematologic (including agranulocytosis, thrombocytopenia), and renal toxicities may occur after multiple doses (<linkHtml href="#LINK_288e647e-d314-4849-9e55-18178c949b0d">5.6</linkHtml>) </item>
                           <item>Hepatotoxicity: Severe, and sometimes fatal, hepatotoxicity has been reported. Discontinue immediately if signs and symptoms of hepatitis occur (<linkHtml href="#LINK_d5113ac6-9819-4e88-9a70-e37a6d8636ae">5.8</linkHtml>) </item>
                           <item>
                              <content styleCode="italics">Clostridium difficile</content>-associated colitis: evaluate if diarrhea occurs (<linkHtml href="#LINK_d2d413d2-2be2-4526-b1a0-06a3e2f20fea">5.9</linkHtml>) </item>
                           <item>Prolongation of the QT interval and isolated cases of torsade de pointes have been reported. Avoid use in patients with known prolongation, those with hypokalemia, and with other drugs that prolong the QT interval (<linkHtml href="#LINK_829decb8-4312-4a6c-9665-e116246457b1">5.10</linkHtml>, <linkHtml href="#LINK_313c8236-c268-4d4e-8899-6c558f8f3a58">8.5</linkHtml>) </item>
                        </list>
                     </text>
                  </highlight>
               </excerpt>
               <component>
                  <section ID="LINK_0991ea01-74a1-403b-851a-36a06ec4872e">
                     <id root="339bd680-4787-48c7-8feb-fb50b9c1017f"/>
                     <code code="42229-5" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="SPL UNCLASSIFIED SECTION"/>
                     <title>
                        <content styleCode="bold">5.1
Disabling and Potentially Irreversible Serious Adverse Reactions Including Tendinitis
and Tendon Rupture, Peripheral Neuropathy, and Central Nervous System Effects</content>
                     </title>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>
                           <content styleCode="xmChange">Fluoroquinolones, including levofloxacin, have been associated with disabling and potentially irreversible serious adverse reactions from different body systems that can occur together in the same patient. Commonly seen adverse reactions include tendinitis, tendon rupture, arthralgia, myalgia, peripheral neuropathy, and central nervous system effects (hallucinations, anxiety, depression, insomnia, severe headaches, and confusion). These reactions can occur within hours to weeks after starting levofloxacin. Patients of any age or without pre-existing risk factors have experienced these adverse reactions [see <content styleCode="bold">WARNINGS AND PRECAUTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_10b867ee-c48f-4bef-8c8f-e9bd9f0ff6ba">5.2</linkHtml>, <linkHtml href="#LINK_7a390283-f0a5-4bf0-9f4a-be9c29fd2fcb">5.3</linkHtml>, <linkHtml href="#LINK_da68872a-681b-4f73-8c30-8e6138e65875">5.4</linkHtml>)</content>].</content>
                        </paragraph>
                        <paragraph>
                           <content styleCode="xmChange">Discontinue levofloxacin immediately at the first signs or symptoms of any serious adverse reaction. In addition, avoid the use of fluoroquinolones, including levofloxacin, in patients who have experienced any of these serious adverse reactions associated with fluoroquinolones.</content>
                        </paragraph>
                     </text>
                     <effectiveTime value="20160816"/>
                  </section>
               </component>
               <component>
                  <section ID="LINK_10b867ee-c48f-4bef-8c8f-e9bd9f0ff6ba">
                     <id root="90f3d72b-ba79-4507-9db3-bbba513ebf1a"/>
                     <code code="42229-5" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="SPL UNCLASSIFIED SECTION"/>
                     <title>
                        <content styleCode="bold">5.2 Tendinitis and Tendon Rupture</content>
                     </title>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>Fluoroquinolones, including levofloxacin, have been associated with an increased risk of tendinitis and tendon rupture in all ages [see <content styleCode="bold">WARNINGS AND PRECAUTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_0991ea01-74a1-403b-851a-36a06ec4872e">5.1</linkHtml>) </content>and<content styleCode="bold"> ADVERSE REACTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_71d889d7-4aa5-4a9e-be77-c35b07f024d4">6.2</linkHtml>)</content>]. This adverse reaction most frequently involves the Achilles tendon and has also been reported with the rotator cuff (the shoulder), the hand, the biceps, the thumb, and other tendon sites. Tendinitis or tendon rupture can occur within hours or days of starting levofloxacin or as long as several months after completion of fluoroquinolone therapy. Tendinitis and tendon rupture can occur bilaterally.</paragraph>
                        <paragraph> The risk of developing fluoroquinolone-associated tendinitis and tendon rupture is increased in patients over 60 years of age, in those taking corticosteroid drugs, and in patients with kidney, heart or lung transplants. Other factors that may independently increase the risk of tendon rupture include strenuous physical activity, renal failure, and previous tendon disorders such as rheumatoid arthritis. Tendinitis and tendon rupture have been reported in patients taking fluoroquinolones who do not have the above risk factors. Discontinue levofloxacin immediately if the patient experiences pain, swelling, inflammation or rupture of a tendon. Patients should be advised to rest at the first sign of tendinitis or tendon rupture, and to contact their healthcare provider regarding changing to a non-quinolone antimicrobial drug. Avoid levofloxacin in patients who have a history of tendon disorders or tendon rupture [see <content styleCode="bold">ADVERSE REACTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_bdbfd5b5-5f2a-4f7b-a066-c2a95c73d8d9">6.3</linkHtml>)</content>; <content styleCode="bold">PATIENT COUNSELING INFORMATION (<linkHtml href="#LINK_683559af-c23d-4c3a-9d96-d55a6eeecd6e">17.3</linkHtml>)</content>].</paragraph>
                     </text>
                     <effectiveTime value="20160816"/>
                  </section>
               </component>
               <component>
                  <section ID="LINK_7a390283-f0a5-4bf0-9f4a-be9c29fd2fcb">
                     <id root="5a6b68de-ad8f-4dee-944d-ba8d413c11a7"/>
                     <code code="42229-5" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="SPL UNCLASSIFIED SECTION"/>
                     <title>
                        <content styleCode="bold">5.3 Peripheral Neuropathy</content>
                     </title>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>Fluoroquinolones, including levofloxacin, have been associated with an increased risk of peripheral neuropathy. Cases of sensory or sensorimotor axonal polyneuropathy affecting small and/or large axons resulting in paresthesias, hypoesthesias, dysesthesias and weakness have been reported in patients receiving fluoroquinolones, including levofloxacin. Symptoms may occur soon after initiation of levofloxacin and may be irreversible in some patients [see <content styleCode="bold">Warnings and Precautions (<linkHtml href="#LINK_0991ea01-74a1-403b-851a-36a06ec4872e">5.1</linkHtml>) </content>and<content styleCode="bold"> Adverse Reactions (<linkHtml href="#LINK_38344cce-d4d7-4566-8a4a-28ff594d1902">6.1</linkHtml>, <linkHtml href="#LINK_71d889d7-4aa5-4a9e-be77-c35b07f024d4">6.2</linkHtml>)</content>]. </paragraph>
                        <paragraph>Discontinue levofloxacin immediately if the patient experiences symptoms of neuropathy including pain, burning, tingling, numbness, and/or weakness or other alterations of sensation including light touch, pain, temperature, position sense, and vibratory sensation. Avoid fluoroquinolones, including levofloxacin, in patients who have previously experienced peripheral neuropathy [see <content styleCode="bold">ADVERSE REACTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_9144420f-d7c5-4c9d-b8f4-8e5ce7f9909b">6</linkHtml>)</content>; <content styleCode="bold">PATIENT COUNSELING INFORMATION (<linkHtml href="#LINK_683559af-c23d-4c3a-9d96-d55a6eeecd6e">17.3</linkHtml>)</content>]<content styleCode="italics">.</content>
                        </paragraph>
                     </text>
                     <effectiveTime value="20160816"/>
                  </section>
               </component>
               <component>
                  <section ID="LINK_da68872a-681b-4f73-8c30-8e6138e65875">
                     <id root="d14ac80b-45c8-4a65-99df-fbf72559c15e"/>
                     <code code="42229-5" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="SPL UNCLASSIFIED SECTION"/>
                     <title>
                        <content styleCode="bold">5.4 Central Nervous System Effects</content>
                     </title>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>Fluoroquinolones, including levofloxacin, have been associated with an increased risk of central nervous system (CNS) effects, including convulsions, toxic psychoses, increased intracranial pressure (including pseudotumor cerebri). Fluoroquinolones may also cause central nervous system stimulation which may lead to tremors, restlessness, anxiety, lightheadedness, confusion, hallucinations, paranoia, depression, nightmares, insomnia, and, rarely, suicidal thoughts or acts. These reactions may occur following the first dose. If these reactions occur in patients receiving levofloxacin, discontinue levofloxacin and institute appropriate measures. As with other fluoroquinolones, levofloxacin should be used with caution in patients with a known or suspected central nervous system (CNS) disorder that may predispose them to seizures or lower the seizure threshold (e.g., severe cerebral arteriosclerosis, epilepsy) or in the presence of other risk factors that may predispose them to seizures or lower the seizure threshold (e.g., certain drug therapy, renal dysfunction).Â [see <content styleCode="bold">ADVERSE REACTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_9144420f-d7c5-4c9d-b8f4-8e5ce7f9909b">6</linkHtml>)</content>; <content styleCode="bold">DRUG INTERACTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_30a94422-889f-4ef0-b3fa-2be80926bc8f">7.4</linkHtml>, <linkHtml href="#LINK_c22078fc-57b5-4b7c-9f61-efec69ff90f4">7.5</linkHtml>)</content>; <content styleCode="bold">PATIENT COUNSELING INFORMATION (<linkHtml href="#LINK_683559af-c23d-4c3a-9d96-d55a6eeecd6e">17.3</linkHtml>)</content>].</paragraph>
                     </text>
                     <effectiveTime value="20160815"/>
                  </section>
               </component>
               <component>
                  <section ID="LINK_aaee3dd2-757e-45de-815b-91e5d8b415e6">
                     <id root="d9bd12a0-844c-4643-aac6-4fbf479651d6"/>
                     <code code="42229-5" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="SPL UNCLASSIFIED SECTION"/>
                     <title>
                        <content styleCode="bold">5.5 Exacerbation of Myasthenia Gravis</content>
                     </title>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>Fluoroquinolones, including levofloxacin, have neuromuscular blocking activity and may exacerbate muscle weakness in patients with myasthenia gravis. Postmarketing serious adverse reactions including deaths and requirement for ventilatory support, have been associated with fluoroquinolone use in patients with myasthenia gravis. Avoid levofloxacin in patients with a known history of myasthenia gravis [see <content styleCode="bold">ADVERSE REACTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_bdbfd5b5-5f2a-4f7b-a066-c2a95c73d8d9">6.3</linkHtml>)</content>; <content styleCode="bold">PATIENT COUNSELING INFORMATION (<linkHtml href="#LINK_683559af-c23d-4c3a-9d96-d55a6eeecd6e">17.3</linkHtml>)</content>].</paragraph>
                     </text>
                     <effectiveTime value="20160815"/>
                  </section>
               </component>
               <component>
                  <section ID="LINK_288e647e-d314-4849-9e55-18178c949b0d">
                     <id root="3b10e1bc-6d55-481a-9543-9a932d20cf3f"/>
                     <code code="42229-5" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="SPL UNCLASSIFIED SECTION"/>
                     <title>
                        <content styleCode="bold">5.6 Other Serious and Sometimes Fatal Adverse Reactions</content>
                     </title>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>Other serious and sometimes fatal adverse reactions, some due to hypersensitivity, and some due to uncertain etiology, have been reported rarely in patients receiving therapy with fluoroquinolones, including levofloxacin. These events may be severe and generally occur following the administration of multiple doses. Clinical manifestations may include one or more of the following: </paragraph>
                        <list listType="unordered" styleCode="Disk">
                           <item>fever, rash, or severe dermatologic reactions (e.g., toxic epidermal necrolysis, Stevens-Johnson Syndrome); </item>
                           <item>vasculitis; arthralgia; myalgia; serum sickness; </item>
                           <item>allergic pneumonitis; </item>
                           <item>interstitial nephritis; acute renal insufficiency or failure; </item>
                           <item>hepatitis; jaundice; acute hepatic necrosis or failure; </item>
                           <item>anemia, including hemolytic and aplastic; thrombocytopenia, including thrombotic thrombocytopenic purpura; leukopenia; agranulocytosis; pancytopenia; and/or other hematologic abnormalities. </item>
                        </list>
                        <paragraph>Discontinue levofloxacin immediately at the first appearance of skin rash, jaundice, or any other sign of hypersensitivity and institute supportive measures [see <content styleCode="bold">ADVERSE REACTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_9144420f-d7c5-4c9d-b8f4-8e5ce7f9909b">6</linkHtml>)</content>; <content styleCode="bold">PATIENT COUNSELING INFORMATION (<linkHtml href="#LINK_683559af-c23d-4c3a-9d96-d55a6eeecd6e">17.3</linkHtml>)</content>]<content styleCode="italics">.</content>
                        </paragraph>
                     </text>
                     <effectiveTime value="20160816"/>
                  </section>
               </component>
               <component>
                  <section ID="LINK_1bd7e834-3bbd-47b6-9794-f13e51b6b1e7">
                     <id root="e7213ecf-45e8-42d5-93f5-40fb191e289f"/>
                     <code code="42229-5" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="SPL UNCLASSIFIED SECTION"/>
                     <title>
                        <content styleCode="bold">5.7 Hypersensitivity Reactions</content>
                     </title>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>Serious and occasionally fatal hypersensitivity and/or anaphylactic reactions have been reported in patients receiving therapy with fluoroquinolones, including levofloxacin. These reactions often occur following the first dose. Some reactions have been accompanied by cardiovascular collapse, hypotension/shock, seizure, loss of consciousness, tingling, angioedema (including tongue, laryngeal, throat, or facial edema/swelling), airway obstruction (including bronchospasm, shortness of breath, and acute respiratory distress), dyspnea, urticaria, itching, and other serious skin reactions. Levofloxacin should be discontinued immediately at the first appearance of a skin rash or any other sign of hypersensitivity. Serious acute hypersensitivity reactions may require treatment with epinephrine and other resuscitative measures, including oxygen, intravenous fluids, antihistamines, corticosteroids, pressor amines, and airway management, as clinically indicated [see <content styleCode="bold">ADVERSE REACTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_9144420f-d7c5-4c9d-b8f4-8e5ce7f9909b">6</linkHtml>)</content>; <content styleCode="bold">PATIENT COUNSELING INFORMATION (<linkHtml href="#LINK_683559af-c23d-4c3a-9d96-d55a6eeecd6e">17.3</linkHtml>)</content>]<content styleCode="italics">. </content>
                        </paragraph>
                     </text>
                     <effectiveTime value="20160815"/>
                  </section>
               </component>
               <component>
                  <section ID="LINK_d5113ac6-9819-4e88-9a70-e37a6d8636ae">
                     <id root="4ddb55ae-9ffc-44d3-b743-f493e744191c"/>
                     <code code="42229-5" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="SPL UNCLASSIFIED SECTION"/>
                     <title>
                        <content styleCode="bold">5.8 Hepatotoxicity</content>
                     </title>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>Post-marketing reports of severe hepatotoxicity (including acute hepatitis and fatal events) have been received for patients treated with levofloxacin. No evidence of serious drug-associated hepatotoxicity was detected in clinical trials of over 7,000 patients. Severe hepatotoxicity generally occurred within 14 days of initiation of therapy and most cases occurred within 6 days. Most cases of severe hepatotoxicity were not associated with hypersensitivity [see <content styleCode="bold">WARNINGS AND PRECAUTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_288e647e-d314-4849-9e55-18178c949b0d">5.6</linkHtml>)</content>]. The majority of fatal hepatotoxicity reports occurred in patients 65 years of age or older and most were not associated with hypersensitivity. Levofloxacin should be discontinued immediately if the patient develops signs and symptoms of hepatitis [see <content styleCode="bold">ADVERSE REACTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_9144420f-d7c5-4c9d-b8f4-8e5ce7f9909b">6</linkHtml>)</content>; <content styleCode="bold">PATIENT COUNSELING INFORMATION (<linkHtml href="#LINK_683559af-c23d-4c3a-9d96-d55a6eeecd6e">17.3</linkHtml>)</content>]. </paragraph>
                     </text>
                     <effectiveTime value="20160815"/>
                  </section>
               </component>
               <component>
                  <section ID="LINK_d2d413d2-2be2-4526-b1a0-06a3e2f20fea">
                     <id root="16d0fa51-3ee1-4b7d-9452-567531729479"/>
                     <code code="42229-5" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="SPL UNCLASSIFIED SECTION"/>
                     <title>
                        <content styleCode="bold">5.9 <content styleCode="italics">Clostridium difficile</content>-Associated Diarrhea</content>
                     </title>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>
                           <content styleCode="italics">Clostridium difficile</content>-associated diarrhea (CDAD) has been reported with use of nearly all antibacterial agents, including levofloxacin, and may range in severity from mild diarrhea to fatal colitis. Treatment with antibacterial agents alters the normal flora of the colon leading to overgrowth of <content styleCode="italics">C. difficile</content>. </paragraph>
                        <paragraph>
                           <content styleCode="italics">C. difficile </content>produces toxins A and B which contribute to the development of CDAD. Hypertoxin producing strains of <content styleCode="italics">C.Â difficile </content>cause increased morbidity and mortality, as these infections can be refractory to antimicrobial therapy and may require colectomy. CDAD must be considered in all patients who present with diarrhea following antibiotic use. Careful medical history is necessary since CDAD has been reported to occur over two months after the administration of antibacterial agents. </paragraph>
                        <paragraph> If CDAD is suspected or confirmed, ongoing antibiotic use not directed against <content styleCode="italics">C. difficile </content>may need to be discontinued. Appropriate fluid and electrolyte management, protein supplementation, antibiotic treatment of <content styleCode="italics">C. difficile,</content> and surgical evaluation should be instituted as clinically indicated [see <content styleCode="bold">ADVERSE REACTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_71d889d7-4aa5-4a9e-be77-c35b07f024d4">6.2</linkHtml>)</content>; <content styleCode="bold">PATIENT COUNSELING INFORMATION (<linkHtml href="#LINK_683559af-c23d-4c3a-9d96-d55a6eeecd6e">17.3</linkHtml>)</content>]<content styleCode="italics">. </content>
                        </paragraph>
                     </text>
                     <effectiveTime value="20160815"/>
                  </section>
               </component>
               <component>
                  <section ID="LINK_829decb8-4312-4a6c-9665-e116246457b1">
                     <id root="b9e7455c-a75b-48a9-9c23-9f9f51ebb7a0"/>
                     <code code="42229-5" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="SPL UNCLASSIFIED SECTION"/>
                     <title>
                        <content styleCode="bold">5.10 Prolongation of the QT Interval</content>
                     </title>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>Some fluoroquinolones, including levofloxacin, have been associated with prolongation of the QT interval on the electrocardiogram and infrequent cases of arrhythmia. Rare cases of torsade de pointes have been spontaneously reported during postmarketing surveillance in patients receiving fluoroquinolones, including levofloxacin. Levofloxacin should be avoided in patients with known prolongation of the QT interval, patients with uncorrected hypokalemia, and patients receiving Class IA (quinidine, procainamide), or Class III (amiodarone, sotalol) antiarrhythmic agents. Elderly patients may be more susceptible to drug-associated effects on the QT intervalÂ [see <content styleCode="bold">ADVERSE REACTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_bdbfd5b5-5f2a-4f7b-a066-c2a95c73d8d9">6.3</linkHtml>)</content>; <content styleCode="bold">USE IN SPECIFIC POPULATIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_313c8236-c268-4d4e-8899-6c558f8f3a58">8.5</linkHtml>)</content>; and <content styleCode="bold">PATIENT COUNSELING INFORMATION (<linkHtml href="#LINK_683559af-c23d-4c3a-9d96-d55a6eeecd6e">17.3</linkHtml>)</content>]<content styleCode="italics">. </content>
                        </paragraph>
                     </text>
                     <effectiveTime value="20160815"/>
                  </section>
               </component>
               <component>
                  <section ID="LINK_550c6231-6cb2-42e4-9049-2c1d5afddcab">
                     <id root="1ca65c0d-0e39-4470-92d9-46a87ff82f2a"/>
                     <code code="42229-5" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="SPL UNCLASSIFIED SECTION"/>
                     <title>
                        <content styleCode="bold">5.11 Musculoskeletal Disorders in Pediatric Patients and Arthropathic Effects in Animals</content>
                     </title>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>Levofloxacin is indicated in pediatric patients (6 months of age and older) only for the prevention of inhalational anthrax (post-exposure) and for plagueÂ [see <content styleCode="bold">INDICATIONS AND USAGE (<linkHtml href="#LINK_8eacae28-b314-4a45-9357-42bea6ffb8d8">1.7</linkHtml>, <linkHtml href="#LINK_5f968ece-0395-425c-90a2-175b5911e7a8">1.8</linkHtml>)</content>]. An increased incidence of musculoskeletal disorders (arthralgia, arthritis, tendinopathy, and gait abnormality) compared to controls has been observed in pediatric patients receiving levofloxacin [see <content styleCode="bold">USE IN SPECIFIC POPULATIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_2de9de63-7015-4729-94e1-92c1738623fa">8.4</linkHtml>)</content>].</paragraph>
                        <paragraph>In immature rats and dogs, the oral and intravenous administration of levofloxacin resulted in increased osteochondrosis. Histopathological examination of the weight-bearing joints of immature dogs dosed with levofloxacin revealed persistent lesions of the cartilage. Other fluoroquinolones also produce similar erosions in the weight-bearing joints and other signs of arthropathy in immature animals of various species [see <content styleCode="bold">Animal Toxicology and/or Pharmacology (<linkHtml href="#LINK_5db87c74-a8b2-48e6-84c5-01dd8fb44315">13.2</linkHtml>)</content>].</paragraph>
                     </text>
                     <effectiveTime value="20160815"/>
                  </section>
               </component>
               <component>
                  <section ID="LINK_6accbecc-fe38-495e-9d5a-282edd2a21db">
                     <id root="6b20b462-c31c-4077-9930-cac343f3a713"/>
                     <code code="42229-5" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="SPL UNCLASSIFIED SECTION"/>
                     <title>
                        <content styleCode="bold">5.12 Blood Glucose Disturbances</content>
                     </title>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>As with other fluoroquinolones, disturbances of blood glucose, including symptomatic hyper- and hypoglycemia, have been reported with levofloxacin, usually in diabetic patients receiving concomitant treatment with an oral hypoglycemic agent (e.g., glyburide) or with insulin. In these patients, careful monitoring of blood glucose is recommended. If a hypoglycemic reaction occurs in a patient being treated with levofloxacin, levofloxacin should be discontinued and appropriate therapy should be initiated immediately [see <content styleCode="bold">ADVERSE REACTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_71d889d7-4aa5-4a9e-be77-c35b07f024d4">6.2</linkHtml>)</content>; <content styleCode="bold">DRUG INTERACTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_f33fa37c-013c-45e1-b312-279c547469a4">7.3</linkHtml>)</content>; <content styleCode="bold">PATIENT COUNSELING INFORMATION (<linkHtml href="#LINK_59fd1e07-797c-41c8-82d3-b6597c3fddc1">17.4</linkHtml>)</content>].</paragraph>
                     </text>
                     <effectiveTime value="20160815"/>
                  </section>
               </component>
               <component>
                  <section ID="LINK_237163c2-7d5c-47cc-927d-00589d6803d1">
                     <id root="0c20660b-52ae-41e1-8065-ebda9a34f898"/>
                     <code code="42229-5" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="SPL UNCLASSIFIED SECTION"/>
                     <title>
                        <content styleCode="bold">5.13 Photosensitivity/Phototoxicity</content>
                     </title>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>Moderate to severe photosensitivity/phototoxicity reactions, the latter of which may manifest as exaggerated sunburn reactions (e.g., burning, erythema, exudation, vesicles, blistering, edema) involving areas exposed to light (typically the face, âVâ area of the neck, extensor surfaces of the forearms, dorsa of the hands), can be associated with the use of fluoroquinolones after sun or UV light exposure. Therefore, excessive exposure to these sources of light should be avoided. Drug therapy should be discontinued if photosensitivity/phototoxicity occurs [see <content styleCode="bold">ADVERSE REACTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_bdbfd5b5-5f2a-4f7b-a066-c2a95c73d8d9">6.3</linkHtml>)</content>; <content styleCode="bold">PATIENT COUNSELING INFORMATION (<linkHtml href="#LINK_683559af-c23d-4c3a-9d96-d55a6eeecd6e">17.3</linkHtml>)</content>]. </paragraph>
                     </text>
                     <effectiveTime value="20160815"/>
                  </section>
               </component>
               <component>
                  <section ID="LINK_5609ee2e-b56d-4838-8886-05b1421a5efc">
                     <id root="1e8a642e-4522-4405-8b7a-ea31efe32728"/>
                     <code code="42229-5" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="SPL UNCLASSIFIED SECTION"/>
                     <title>
                        <content styleCode="bold">5.14 Development of Drug Resistant Bacteria</content>
                     </title>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>Prescribing levofloxacin in the absence of a proven or strongly suspected bacterial infection or a prophylactic indication is unlikely to provide benefit to the patient and increases the risk of the development of drugâresistant bacteria [see <content styleCode="bold">PATIENT COUNSELING INFORMATION (<linkHtml href="#LINK_372f9005-d57d-43db-9534-f6fedc9f4dc7">17.2</linkHtml>)</content>].</paragraph>
                     </text>
                     <effectiveTime value="20160815"/>
                  </section>
               </component>
            </section>
         </component>
         <component>
            <section ID="LINK_9144420f-d7c5-4c9d-b8f4-8e5ce7f9909b">
               <id root="8ff5147a-d111-4778-bc44-8e363d7fa575"/>
               <code code="34084-4" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="ADVERSE REACTIONS SECTION"/>
               <title>6 ADVERSE REACTIONS</title>
               <effectiveTime value="20160815"/>
               <excerpt>
                  <highlight>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>The most common reactions (â¥ 3%) were nausea, headache, diarrhea, insomnia, constipation and dizziness (<linkHtml href="#LINK_71d889d7-4aa5-4a9e-be77-c35b07f024d4">6.2</linkHtml>).</paragraph>
                        <paragraph>
                           <content styleCode="bold">To report SUSPECTED ADVERSE REACTIONS, contact West-Ward PharmaceuticalsÂ Corp.Â at 1-877-233-2001, or theÂ FDA at 1-800-FDA-1088 or <linkHtml href="#medwatch">www.fda.gov/medwatch</linkHtml>.</content>

                  <section ID="LINK_38344cce-d4d7-4566-8a4a-28ff594d1902">
                     <id root="c8350760-f089-4e1b-b324-48ff2e91b61b"/>
                     <code code="42229-5" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="SPL UNCLASSIFIED SECTION"/>
                     <title>
                        <content styleCode="bold">6.1 Serious and Otherwise Important Adverse Reactions</content>
                     </title>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>The following serious and otherwise important adverse drug reactions are discussed in greater detail in other sections of labeling:</paragraph>
                        <list listType="unordered" styleCode="Disk">
                           <item>Disabling and Potentially Irreversible Serious Adverse Reactions [see <content styleCode="bold">WARNINGS AND PRECAUTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_0991ea01-74a1-403b-851a-36a06ec4872e">5.1</linkHtml>)</content>]</item>
                           <item>Tendinitis and Tendon Rupture [see <content styleCode="bold">WARNINGS AND PRECAUTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_10b867ee-c48f-4bef-8c8f-e9bd9f0ff6ba">5.2</linkHtml>)</content>]</item>
                           <item>Peripheral Neuropathy [see <content styleCode="bold">WARNINGS AND PRECAUTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_7a390283-f0a5-4bf0-9f4a-be9c29fd2fcb">5.3</linkHtml>)</content>]</item>
                           <item>Central Nervous System Effects [see <content styleCode="bold">WARNINGS AND PRECAUTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_da68872a-681b-4f73-8c30-8e6138e65875">5.4</linkHtml>)</content>]</item>
                           <item>Exacerbation of Myasthenia Gravis [see <content styleCode="bold">WARNINGS AND PRECAUTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_aaee3dd2-757e-45de-815b-91e5d8b415e6">5.5</linkHtml>)</content>]</item>

                           <item>Hypersensitivity Reactions [see <content styleCode="bold">WARNINGS AND PRECAUTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_1bd7e834-3bbd-47b6-9794-f13e51b6b1e7">5.7</linkHtml>)</content>]</item>
                           <item>Hepatotoxicity [see <content styleCode="bold">WARNINGS AND PRECAUTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_d5113ac6-9819-4e88-9a70-e37a6d8636ae">5.8</linkHtml>)</content>]</item>
                           <item>Clostridium difficile-Associated Diarrhea [see <content styleCode="bold">WARNINGS AND PRECAUTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_d2d413d2-2be2-4526-b1a0-06a3e2f20fea">5.9</linkHtml>)</content>] </item>
                           <item>Prolongation of the QT Interval [see <content styleCode="bold">WARNINGS AND PRECAUTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_829decb8-4312-4a6c-9665-e116246457b1">5.10</linkHtml>)</content>]</item>
                           <item>Musculoskeletal Disorders in Pediatric Patients [see <content styleCode="bold">WARNINGS AND PRECAUTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_550c6231-6cb2-42e4-9049-2c1d5afddcab">5.11</linkHtml>)</content>]</item>
                           <item>Blood Glucose Disturbances [see <content styleCode="bold">WARNINGS AND PRECAUTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_6accbecc-fe38-495e-9d5a-282edd2a21db">5.12</linkHtml>)</content>]</item>
                           <item>Photosensitivity/Phototoxicity [see <content styleCode="bold">WARNINGS AND PRECAUTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_237163c2-7d5c-47cc-927d-00589d6803d1">5.13</linkHtml>)</content>]</item>

                        </list>
                        <paragraph>Hypotension has been associated with rapid or bolus intravenous infusion of levofloxacin. Levofloxacin should be infused slowly over 60 to 90 minutes, depending on dosage [see <content styleCode="bold">DOSAGE AND ADMINISTRATION (<linkHtml href="#LINK_c66ccf10-2cdb-4177-a8c1-87592e9d2b62">2.5</linkHtml>)</content>].</paragraph>
                        <paragraph>Crystalluria and cylindruria have been reported with quinolones, including levofloxacin. Therefore, adequate hydration of patients receiving levofloxacin should be maintained to prevent the formation of a highly concentrated urine [see <content styleCode="bold">DOSAGE AND ADMINISTRATION (<linkHtml href="#LINK_c66ccf10-2cdb-4177-a8c1-87592e9d2b62">2.5</linkHtml>)</content>].</paragraph>
                     </text>

               <component>
                  <section ID="LINK_71d889d7-4aa5-4a9e-be77-c35b07f024d4">
                     <id root="88e7f517-c5bd-493d-a9e4-d691c4a4bfa3"/>
                     <code code="42229-5" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="SPL UNCLASSIFIED SECTION"/>
                     <title>
                        <content styleCode="bold">6.2 Clinical Trial Experience</content>
                     </title>
                     <text>
                        <paragraph>Because clinical trials are conducted under widely varying conditions, adverse reaction rates observed in the clinical trials of a drug cannot be directly compared to rates in the clinical trials of another drug and may not reflect the rates observed in practice.</paragraph>
                        <paragraph>The data described below reflect exposure to levofloxacin in 7537 patients in 29 pooled Phase 3 clinical trials. The population studied had a mean age of 50 years (approximately 74% of the population was &lt; 65 years of age), 50% were male, 71% were Caucasian, 19% were Black. Patients were treated with levofloxacin for a wide variety of infectious diseases [see <content styleCode="bold">INDICATIONS AND USAGE (<linkHtml href="#LINK_89e216a7-8b92-49d4-ada0-96ac04abc313">1</linkHtml>)</content>]. Patients received levofloxacin doses of 750 mg once daily, 250 mg once daily, or 500 mg once or twice daily. Treatment duration was usually 3â14 days, and the mean number of days on therapy was 10 days.</paragraph>
                        <paragraph>The overall incidence, type and distribution of adverse reactions was similar in patients receiving levofloxacin doses of 750 mg once daily, 250 mg once daily, and 500Â mg once or twice daily. Discontinuation of levofloxacin due to adverse drug reactions occurred in 4.3% of patients overall, 3.8% of patients treated with the 250Â mg and 500Â mg doses and 5.4% of patients treated with the 750 mg dose. The most common adverse drug reactions leading to discontinuation with the 250 and 500 mg doses were gastrointestinal (1.4%), primarily nausea (0.6%); vomiting (0.4%); dizziness (0.3%); and headache (0.2%). The most common adverse drug reactions leading to discontinuation with the 750 mg dose were gastrointestinal (1.2%), primarily nausea (0.6%), vomiting (0.5%); dizziness (0.3%); and headache (0.3%).</paragraph>
                        <paragraph>Adverse reactions occurring in â¥ 1% of levofloxacin-treated patients and less common adverse reactions, occurring in 0.1 to &lt; 1% of levofloxacin-treated patients, are shown in <content styleCode="bold">Table 4 </content>and <content styleCode="bold">Table 5</content>, respectively. The most common adverse drug reactions (â¥ 3%) are nausea, headache, diarrhea, insomnia, constipation, and dizziness.</paragraph>

                                    <paragraph>urticaria [see <content styleCode="bold">WARNINGS AND PRECAUTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_1bd7e834-3bbd-47b6-9794-f13e51b6b1e7">5.7</linkHtml>)</content>]</paragraph>
                                 </td>
                              </tr>
                              <tr>
                                 <td styleCode="     Botrule          Toprule         Lrule          Rrule     " valign="top">
                                    <paragraph>
                                       <content styleCode="bold">Musculoskeletal and Connective Tissue Disorders</content>
                                    </paragraph>
                                 </td>
                                 <td styleCode="     Botrule          Toprule         Lrule          Rrule     " valign="top">
                                    <paragraph>arthralgia<br/>tendinitis<br/>[see <content styleCode="bold">WARNINGS AND PRECAUTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_550c6231-6cb2-42e4-9049-2c1d5afddcab">5.11</linkHtml>)</content>] <br/>myalgia<br/>skeletal pain </paragraph>
                                 </td>
                              </tr>
                              <tr>
                                 <td styleCode="     Botrule          Toprule         Lrule          Rrule     " valign="top">
                                    <paragraph>
                                       <content styleCode="bold">Renal and Urinary Disorders</content>
                                    </paragraph>
                                 </td>
                                 <td styleCode="     Botrule          Toprule         Lrule          Rrule     " valign="top">
                                    <paragraph>abnormal renal function<br/>acute renal failure [see <content styleCode="bold">WARNINGS AND PRECAUTIONS (<linkHtml href="#LINK_288e647e-d314-4849-9e55-18178c949b0d">5.6</linkHtml>)</content>]</paragraph>
                                 </td>
                              </tr>
                           </tbody>
                        </table>
                        <paragraph>In clinical trials using multiple-dose therapy, ophthalmologic abnormalities, including cataracts and multiple punctate lenticular opacities, have been noted in patients undergoing treatment with quinolones, including levofloxacin. The relationship of the drugs to these events is not presently established.</paragraph>
                     </text>

               <id root="84b6764f-a702-41b8-97ca-bfb7b38c2337"/>
               <code code="34073-7" codeSystem="2.16.840.1.113883.6.1" displayName="DRUG INTERACTIONS SECTION"/>
               <title>7 DRUG INTERACTIONS</title>
               <effectiveTime value="20160816"/>
               <excerpt>
                  <highlight>
                     <text>

                                 <td styleCode="     Botrule          Toprule         Lrule          Rrule     " valign="top">

                                 </td>

                                    <paragraph>Absorption of levofloxacin is decreased when the tablet or oral solution formulation is taken within 2 hours of these products.
